<!-- link2 "Item&nbsp;2.02 Results of Operations and Financial Condition." -->
<DIV align="left"><A NAME="000"></A></DIV>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Item&nbsp;2.02 Results of Operations and Financial Condition.</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">On September&nbsp;21, 2004, The Goldman Sachs Group, Inc. (the Registrant)
reported its earnings for its fiscal third quarter ended August&nbsp;27, 2004. A
copy of the Registrant&#146;s press release containing this information is being
furnished as Exhibit&nbsp;99.1 to this Report on Form 8-K and is incorporated herein
by reference.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">The information furnished pursuant to this Item&nbsp;2.02, including Exhibit
99.1, shall not be deemed &#147;filed&#148; for purposes of Section&nbsp;18 of the Securities
Exchange Act of 1934 (the Exchange Act) or otherwise subject to the liabilities
under that Section and shall not be deemed to be incorporated by reference into
any filing of the Registrant under the Securities Act of 1933 or the Exchange
Act.

<!-- link2 "Item&nbsp;8.01 Other Events." -->
<DIV align="left"><A NAME="001"></A></DIV>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Item&nbsp;8.01 Other Events.</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">On September&nbsp;21, 2004, the Registrant reported net earnings of $879
million for its fiscal third quarter ended August&nbsp;27, 2004. Diluted earnings
per share were $1.74 compared with $1.32 for the third quarter of 2003 and
$2.31 for the second quarter of 2004. Annualized return on average tangible
shareholders&#146; equity <SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(1)</SUP> was 19.2% for the third quarter of 2004 and 25.3% for
the first nine months of 2004. Annualized return on average shareholders&#146;
equity was 15.1% for the third quarter of 2004 and 19.8% for the first nine
months of 2004.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Net Revenues</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><U><B>Investment Banking</B></U>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Net revenues in Investment Banking were $890&nbsp;million compared with $687
million for the third quarter of 2003 and $953&nbsp;million for the second quarter
of 2004. Net revenues in Financial Advisory were $451&nbsp;million compared with
$304&nbsp;million for the same period last year, primarily reflecting an increase in
industry-wide completed mergers and acquisitions. Net revenues in the firm&#146;s
Underwriting business were $439&nbsp;million compared with $383&nbsp;million for the same
2003 period, due to higher net revenues from debt new issuances and equity
underwriting activity, partially offset by lower net revenues from convertible
issuances. The firm&#146;s investment banking backlog declined during the quarter.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><U><B>Trading and Principal Investments</B></U>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Net revenues in Trading and Principal Investments were $2.70&nbsp;billion, 15%
above the third quarter of 2003 and 26% below the second quarter of 2004. The
decline compared with the second quarter of 2004 was primarily due to changes
in the fair value of the firm&#146;s investment in the convertible preferred stock
of Sumitomo Mitsui Financial Group, Inc. (SMFG).


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Net revenues in Fixed Income, Currency and Commodities (FICC)&nbsp;were $1.87
billion compared with $879&nbsp;million for the third quarter of 2003. The increase
was primarily driven by strong results in mortgages, commodities, credit
products and interest rate products. Results in


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">- 2 -
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">currencies were only slightly higher than the difficult third quarter of
2003. Despite a flattening yield curve in the quarter, customer-driven
activity in FICC remained generally strong, particularly in commodities, where
energy prices generally rose.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Net revenues in Equities of $910&nbsp;million decreased 17% compared with the
third quarter of 2003, as the business operated in a less favorable
environment, generally characterized by flat to declining equity prices,
further reductions in market volatility and lower customer-driven activity.
Results in the firm&#146;s principal strategies business <SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(2)</SUP> declined across most
sectors compared with the third quarter of 2003. In addition, net revenues in
the firm&#146;s equities products group <SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(3)</SUP> were lower in both shares and
derivatives.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Principal Investments recorded negative net revenues of $79&nbsp;million,
primarily due to an unrealized loss of $245&nbsp;million (as compared with a $561
million unrealized gain in the second quarter of 2004) related to the firm&#146;s
investment in the convertible preferred stock of SMFG, partially offset by
gains from other corporate and real estate principal investments.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><U><B>Asset Management and Securities Services</B></U>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Net revenues in Asset Management and Securities Services were $941
million, 23% above the third quarter of 2003 and essentially unchanged as
compared with the second quarter of 2004.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Asset Management net revenues of $596&nbsp;million increased 24% compared with
last year&#146;s third quarter, primarily due to higher average assets under
management. During the quarter, assets under management increased $11&nbsp;billion,
reflecting net asset inflows of $10&nbsp;billion across alternative investment,
money market and fixed income assets, as well as market appreciation of $1
billion.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Securities Services net revenues of $345&nbsp;million increased 21% compared
with the third quarter of 2003, primarily due to significantly higher customer
balances in the firm&#146;s securities lending and margin lending businesses.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Expenses</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Operating expenses were $3.24&nbsp;billion, 15% higher than the third quarter
of 2003 and 14% lower than the second quarter of 2004.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Compensation and benefits expenses of $2.26&nbsp;billion increased 19% compared
with the same period last year, commensurate with higher net revenues. The
ratio of compensation and benefits to net revenues was 50% for the first nine
months of 2004, consistent with the first nine months of 2003. Employment
levels increased 4% during the quarter and 4% compared with the end of 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Non-compensation-related expenses of $968&nbsp;million increased 8% compared
with the same period last year, primarily due to higher professional services
and other expenses, principally reflecting higher legal and consulting fees.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">- 3 -
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">The effective income tax rate was 32.3% for the first nine months of 2004,
essentially unchanged from the first half of 2004 and fiscal year 2003.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Capital</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">As of August&nbsp;27, 2004, total capital was $95.19&nbsp;billion, consisting of
$23.51&nbsp;billion in shareholders&#146; equity and
$71.68&nbsp;billion in long-term debt. <SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(4)</SUP>
Book value per share was $48.08 based on common shares outstanding, including
restricted stock units granted to employees with no future service
requirements, of 489.1&nbsp;million at period end. Tangible book value per share
was $38.09.
<SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(1)</sup>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">The firm repurchased 4.8&nbsp;million shares of its common stock during the
quarter at an average price of $89.71 per share. The remaining share
authorization under the firm&#146;s existing common stock repurchase program is 12.0
million shares.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Dividend</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">The Board of Directors of The Goldman Sachs Group, Inc. declared a
dividend of $0.25 per share to be paid on November&nbsp;22, 2004 to common
shareholders of record on October&nbsp;25, 2004.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><U><B>Cautionary Note Regarding Forward-Looking Statements</B></U>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">This Report on Form 8-K contains &#147;forward-looking statements.&#148; These
statements are not historical facts but instead represent only the firm&#146;s
belief regarding future events, many of which, by their nature, are inherently
uncertain and outside of the firm&#146;s control. It is possible that the firm&#146;s
actual results and financial condition may differ, possibly materially, from
the anticipated results and financial condition indicated in these
forward-looking statements. For a discussion of some of the risks and
important factors that could affect the firm&#146;s future results,
see &#147;Business - Certain Factors That May Affect Our
Business&#148; in the firm&#146;s Annual Report on
Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended November&nbsp;28, 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; text-indent: 5%">Statements about the firm&#146;s investment banking transaction backlog also
may constitute forward-looking statements. Such statements are subject to the
risk that the terms of these transactions may be modified or that they may not
be completed at all; therefore, the net revenues that the firm expects to earn
from these transactions may differ, possibly materially, from those currently
expected. Important factors that could result in a modification of the terms
of a transaction or a transaction not being completed include, in the case of
underwriting transactions, a decline in general economic conditions, volatility
in the securities markets generally or an adverse development with respect to
the issuer of the securities and, in the case of financial advisory
transactions, a decline in the securities markets, an adverse development with
respect to a party to the transaction or a failure to obtain a required
regulatory approval. For a discussion of other important factors that could
adversely affect the firm&#146;s investment banking transactions, see
&#147;Business - Certain Factors That May Affect Our Business&#148; in the firm&#146;s Annual Report on
Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended November&nbsp;28, 2003.

    <TD width="4%" nowrap align="left"><SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(1)</SUP></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">Tangible shareholders&#146; equity equals total shareholders&#146; equity
less goodwill and identifiable intangible assets. Management believes
that annualized return on average tangible shareholders&#146; equity is a
meaningful measure of performance because it excludes the portion of
the firm&#146;s shareholders&#146; equity attributable to goodwill and
identifiable intangible assets. As a result, this calculation measures
corporate performance in a manner that treats underlying businesses
consistently, whether they were acquired or developed internally.
Annualized return on average tangible shareholders&#146; equity is computed
by dividing annualized net earnings by average monthly tangible
shareholders&#146; equity. Tangible book value per share is computed by
dividing tangible shareholders&#146; equity by the number of common shares
outstanding, including restricted stock units granted to employees with
no future service requirements. The following table sets forth a
reconciliation of shareholders&#146; equity to tangible shareholders&#146;
equity:</TD>

    <TD width="95%">Long-term debt includes nonrecourse debt of $7.70&nbsp;billion, consisting of
$3.72&nbsp;billion issued by William Street Funding Corporation (a wholly owned
subsidiary of The Goldman Sachs Group, Inc. formed to raise funding to
support loan commitments made by another wholly owned William Street
entity to investment-grade clients), $2.31&nbsp;billion issued by consolidated
variable interest entities and $1.67&nbsp;billion issued by other consolidated
entities, primarily associated with the firm&#146;s ownership of Cogentrix
Energy, Inc. and East Coast Power L.L.C. Nonrecourse debt is debt that
The Goldman Sachs Group, Inc. is not directly or indirectly obligated to
repay through a guarantee, general partnership interest or contractual

    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">Cost of power generation relates to the firm&#146;s ownership of Cogentrix
Energy, Inc., acquired December&nbsp;19, 2003, and East Coast Power L.L.C.
This line includes all of the direct costs of the firm&#146;s consolidated
power plant operations (e.g., fuel, operations and maintenance), as well

&#147;Trading and principal investments.&#148;</TD>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD width="4%" nowrap align="left"><SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(8)</SUP></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">VaR is the potential loss in value of Goldman Sachs&#146; trading positions
due to adverse market movements over a one-day time horizon with a 95%
confidence level. The modeling of the risk characteristics of the firm&#146;s
trading positions involves a number of assumptions and approximations.
While management believes that these assumptions and approximations are
reasonable, there is no uniform industry methodology for estimating VaR,
and different assumptions and/or approximations could produce materially
different VaR estimates. During the fourth quarter of 2003, the firm made
certain changes to its model for calculating VaR. The effect of these
changes was not material and accordingly, prior periods have not been
adjusted. For a further discussion of the calculation of VaR, see Part
II, Item&nbsp;7A &#147;Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures about Market Risk&#148;
in the firm&#146;s Annual Report on Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended
November&nbsp;28, 2003.</TD>
</TR>

<TR><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD width="4%" nowrap align="left"><SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(9)</SUP></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">Equals the difference between firmwide VaR and the sum of the VaRs for
the four risk categories. This effect arises because the four market risk
categories are not perfectly correlated.</TD>
</TR>

<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">


<P align="right" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Exhibit&nbsp;99.1</B>

<DIV align="center">
<TABLE style="font-size: 10pt" cellspacing="0" border="0" cellpadding="0" width="100%">

<!-- Begin Table Head --><TR valign="bottom">
    <TD width="98%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>

<!-- End Table Head -->

<!-- Begin Table Body -->
<TR valign="bottom">
    <TD valign="top"><DIV style="margin-left:0px; text-indent:-0px">The Goldman Sachs Group, Inc.&nbsp;<FONT style="font-size:14pt">|</FONT>&nbsp;85 Broad Street&nbsp;<FONT style="font-size:14pt">|</FONT>&nbsp;New York, New York 10004<br>
</DIV></TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD rowspan="2" align="right" valign="middle"><IMG src="y02301y0230100.gif" alt="(GOLDMAN SACHS LOGO)"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="bottom">
    <TD align="center" valign="top"><DIV style="margin-left:0px; text-indent:-0px"><B>GOLDMAN SACHS REPORTS THIRD QUARTER<br>
EARNINGS PER SHARE OF $1.74</B></DIV></TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>


<!-- End Table Body --></TABLE>
</DIV>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">NEW YORK, September&nbsp;21, 2004 &#151; The Goldman Sachs Group, Inc. (NYSE:GS) today
reported net earnings of $879&nbsp;million for its fiscal third quarter ended August
27, 2004. Diluted earnings per share were $1.74 compared with $1.32 for the
third quarter of 2003 and $2.31 for the second quarter of 2004. Annualized
return on average tangible shareholders&#146; equity <sup>(1)</sup> was 19.2% for the third
quarter of 2004 and 25.3% for the first nine months of 2004. Annualized return
on average shareholders&#146; equity was 15.1% for the third quarter of 2004 and
19.8% for the first nine months of 2004.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Business Highlights</B>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Net Revenues</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B><u>Investment Banking</u></B>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Net revenues in Investment Banking were $890&nbsp;million compared with $687&nbsp;million
for the third quarter of 2003 and $953&nbsp;million for the second quarter of 2004.
Net revenues in Financial Advisory were $451&nbsp;million compared with $304&nbsp;million
for the same period last year, primarily reflecting an increase in
industry-wide completed mergers and acquisitions. Net revenues in the firm&#146;s
Underwriting business were $439&nbsp;million compared with $383&nbsp;million for the same
2003 period, due to higher net revenues from debt new issuances and equity
underwriting activity, partially offset by lower net revenues from convertible
issuances. The firm&#146;s investment banking backlog declined during the quarter<I>.</I>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B><u>Trading and Principal Investments</u></B>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Net revenues in Trading and Principal Investments were $2.70&nbsp;billion, 15% above
the third quarter of 2003 and 26% below the second quarter of 2004. The
decline compared with the second quarter of 2004 was primarily due to changes
in the fair value of the firm&#146;s investment in the convertible preferred stock
of Sumitomo Mitsui Financial Group, Inc. (SMFG).

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Net revenues in FICC were $1.87&nbsp;billion compared with $879&nbsp;million for the
third quarter of 2003. The increase was primarily driven by strong results in
mortgages, commodities, credit products and interest rate products. Results in
currencies were only slightly higher than the difficult third quarter of 2003.
Despite a flattening yield curve in the quarter, customer-driven activity in
FICC remained generally strong, particularly in commodities, where energy
prices generally rose.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Net revenues in Equities of $910&nbsp;million decreased 17% compared with the third
quarter of 2003, as the business operated in a less favorable environment,
generally characterized by flat to declining equity prices, further reductions
in market volatility and lower customer-driven activity. Results in the firm&#146;s
principal strategies business <sup>(3)</sup> declined across most sectors compared with
the third quarter of 2003. In addition, net revenues in the firm&#146;s equities
products group <sup>(4)</sup> were lower in both shares and derivatives.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Principal Investments recorded negative net revenues of $79&nbsp;million, primarily
due to an unrealized loss of $245&nbsp;million (as compared with a $561&nbsp;million
unrealized gain in the second quarter of 2004) related to the firm&#146;s investment
in the convertible preferred stock of SMFG, partially offset by gains from
other corporate and real estate principal investments.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">2
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B><u>Asset Management and Securities Services</u></B>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Net revenues in Asset Management and Securities Services were $941&nbsp;million, 23%
above the third quarter of 2003 and essentially unchanged as compared with the
second quarter of 2004.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Asset Management net revenues of $596&nbsp;million increased 24% compared with last
year&#146;s third quarter, primarily due to higher average assets under management.
During the quarter, assets under management increased $11&nbsp;billion, reflecting
net asset inflows of $10&nbsp;billion across alternative investment, money market
and fixed income assets, as well as market appreciation of $1&nbsp;billion.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Securities Services net revenues of $345&nbsp;million increased 21% compared with
the third quarter of 2003, primarily due to significantly higher customer
balances in the firm&#146;s securities lending and margin lending businesses.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Expenses</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Operating expenses were $3.24&nbsp;billion, 15% higher than the third quarter of
2003 and 14% lower than the second quarter of 2004.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Compensation and benefits expenses of $2.26&nbsp;billion increased 19% compared with
the same period last year, commensurate with higher net revenues. The ratio of
compensation and benefits to net revenues was 50% for the first nine months of
2004, consistent with the first nine months of 2003. Employment levels
increased 4% during the quarter and 4% compared with the end of 2003.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Non-compensation-related expenses of $968&nbsp;million increased 8% compared with
the same period last year, primarily due to higher professional services and
other expenses, principally reflecting higher legal and consulting fees.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The effective income tax rate was 32.3% for the first nine months of 2004,
essentially unchanged from the first half of 2004 and fiscal year 2003.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Capital</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">As of August&nbsp;27, 2004, total capital was $95.19&nbsp;billion, consisting of $23.51
billion in shareholders&#146; equity and $71.68&nbsp;billion in long-term debt. <sup>(5)</sup> Book
value per share was $48.08 based on common shares outstanding, including
restricted stock units granted to employees with no future service
requirements, of 489.1&nbsp;million at period end. Tangible book value per share
was $38.09. <sup>(1)</sup>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The firm repurchased 4.8&nbsp;million shares of its common stock during the quarter
at an average price of $89.71 per share. The remaining share authorization
under the firm&#146;s existing common stock repurchase program is 12.0&nbsp;million
shares.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">3
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Dividend</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Board of Directors of The Goldman Sachs Group, Inc. declared a dividend of
$0.25 per share to be paid on November&nbsp;22, 2004 to common shareholders of
record on October&nbsp;25, 2004.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">*&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;*&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;*


<P align="left" style="font-size: 8pt">Goldman Sachs is a leading global investment banking, securities and investment
management firm that provides a wide range of services worldwide to a
substantial and diversified client base that includes corporations, financial
institutions, governments and high net worth individuals. Founded in 1869, it
is one of the oldest and largest investment banking firms. The firm is
headquartered in New York and maintains offices in London, Frankfurt, Tokyo,
Hong Kong and other major financial centers around the world.

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Footnotes</B>

<P>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 8pt">

<TR valign="top">
    <TD width="4%" nowrap align="left"><SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(1)</SUP></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">Tangible shareholders&#146; equity equals total shareholders&#146; equity less
goodwill and identifiable intangible assets. Management believes that
annualized return on average tangible shareholders&#146; equity is a
meaningful measure of performance because it excludes the portion of the
firm&#146;s shareholders&#146; equity attributable to goodwill and identifiable
intangible assets. As a result, this calculation measures corporate
performance in a manner that treats underlying businesses consistently,
whether they were acquired or developed internally. Annualized return on
average tangible shareholders&#146; equity is computed by dividing annualized
net earnings by average monthly tangible shareholders&#146; equity. Tangible
book value per share is computed by dividing tangible shareholders&#146;
equity by the number of common shares outstanding, including restricted
stock units granted to employees with no future service requirements.
The following table sets forth a reconciliation of shareholders&#146; equity
to tangible shareholders&#146; equity:</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">Long-term debt includes nonrecourse debt of $7.70&nbsp;billion,
consisting of $3.72&nbsp;billion issued by William Street Funding
Corporation (a wholly owned subsidiary of The Goldman Sachs Group, Inc.
formed to raise funding to support loan commitments made by another
wholly owned William Street entity to investment-grade clients), $2.31
billion issued by consolidated variable interest entities and $1.67
billion issued by other consolidated entities, primarily associated
with the firm&#146;s ownership of Cogentrix Energy, Inc. and East Coast
Power L.L.C. Nonrecourse debt is debt that The Goldman Sachs Group,
Inc. is not directly or indirectly obligated to repay through a
guarantee, general partnership interest or contractual arrangement.</TD>
</TR>

<TR><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>

2003. These reclassifications did not affect the firm&#146;s historical

<TR><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>

<TR valign="top">

    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">Cost of power generation relates to the firm&#146;s ownership of
Cogentrix Energy, Inc., acquired December&nbsp;19, 2003, and East Coast
Power L.L.C. This line includes all of the direct costs of the firm&#146;s
consolidated power plant operations (e.g., fuel, operations and
maintenance), as well as the depreciation and amortization associated
with the plants and related contractual assets. Power generation
revenues are included in &#147;Trading and principal investments.&#148;</TD>

<TR><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>

<TR><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD width="4%" nowrap align="left"><SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(9)</SUP></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">VaR is the potential loss in value of Goldman Sachs&#146; trading
positions due to adverse market movements over a one-day time horizon
with a 95% confidence level. The modeling of the risk characteristics
of the firm&#146;s trading positions involves a number of assumptions and
approximations. While management believes that these assumptions and
approximations are reasonable, there is no uniform industry methodology
for estimating VaR, and different assumptions and/or approximations
could produce materially different VaR estimates. During the fourth
quarter of 2003, the firm made certain changes to its model for
calculating VaR. The effect of these changes was not material and
accordingly, prior periods have not been adjusted. For a further
discussion of the calculation of VaR, see Part&nbsp;II, Item&nbsp;7A
&#147;Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures about Market Risk&#148; in the
firm&#146;s Annual Report on Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended November
28, 2003.</TD>
</TR>

<TR><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD width="4%" nowrap align="left"><SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(10)</SUP></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="95%">Equals the difference between firmwide VaR and the sum of the VaRs
for the four risk categories. This effect arises because the four
market risk categories are not perfectly correlated.</TD>
</TR>

<TR><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD width="4%" nowrap align="left"><SUP style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">(11)</SUP></TD>

    <TD width="95%">Substantially all assets under management are valued as of calendar
month end.</TD>

    <TD width="95%">Includes the impact of foreign exchange revaluation on the
investment, for which the firm maintains an economic hedge.</TD>
